<div id="review_1802658549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802658549" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802658549?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17449042-wait-for-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51318038-elena?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51318038-elena?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802658549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12664637255179581033"><b>RE-READ: 06/17/20</b><br/>it's been <b>forever</b> since i last read this<br/><br/>my rating changed to 3 stars<br/><br/>also re reading this review is making me realize that i, in fact, have improved.<br/>2016 me was...not good at writing them LMAO<br/><br/><b>12/26/16: EDIT</b><br/>I'm rating this 4 stars because I'm realizing I'm not enjoying the rest of the books and I'm giving them low ratings. As of now, this is my favorite and I've given 1 and 2 stars to the next books, so this has to be 4 stars.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Leaning back against Cam's chest, I tipped my head b</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12664637255179581033" style="display:none"><b>RE-READ: 06/17/20</b><br />it's been <b>forever</b> since i last read this<br /><br />my rating changed to 3 stars<br /><br />also re reading this review is making me realize that i, in fact, have improved.<br />2016 me was...not good at writing them LMAO<br /><br /><b>12/26/16: EDIT</b><br />I'm rating this 4 stars because I'm realizing I'm not enjoying the rest of the books and I'm giving them low ratings. As of now, this is my favorite and I've given 1 and 2 stars to the next books, so this has to be 4 stars.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Leaning back against Cam's chest, I tipped my head back and I reached up, cupping his cheek. I drew his mouth to mine and kissed him softly. “Thank you.”<br />His lips curved up on one side. “For what?”<br />“For waiting for me.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I actually didn't know J. Lynn was Jennifer L. Armentrout, but because I saw this book in my news feed once and was completely sold out based on the description, I obviously added it to my tbr. Little did I know that this was based on the same author that wrote the <i>Lux</i> series, a series I didn't think I would love and miss so much. Jennifer actually blew me away with this one! I didn't know she wrote NA novels, and I didn't think she would write them this good. Her male leads are just so wonderful and amazing and I really wish they were real. She also gives out female characters that can be relatable and if they aren't, it's really easy to follow the way they're coming from. Although I had some problems with the beginning and Avery (main character) in the beginning, I enjoyed the rest, especially Cameron himself and the way the romance was actually delivered in this which is quite surprising.<br /><br /><i>Wait for You</i> is about 19-year-old college freshman Avery that has just moved away from her Texas to Virginia to run away from her past--the Halloween night that she wishes to never think about again. She knows her parents don't love her, she knows her town hates her, and she knows she doesn't have any friends. Maybe moving into another town will be better and maybe she will be able to live a better life. Avery knows what she wants to do, and she plans on doing it all on time. She plans on getting to class on time, plans on keeping her bracelet on no matter what, and plans on making new friends and having a new and fresh start. What she didn't plan was running her small body into 6'3 college student Cameron Hamilton, known as a college hottie at this new university Avery is at. Little did Avery know that Cameron would come <i>crashing</i> into her life only to make it better.<br /><br />Cameron Hamilton has his own past to run from. It isn't like Avery's, but if you look at it, it has its similarities. He's also known as one of those guys that can get a girl he wants, but with Avery, it's different. Not knowing where Avery comes from and why she acts the way she acts around him, he wants to get to know Avery. She isn't like most girls, and that's what he likes about her. She's quite different. She's never been on a date, never been in a relationship, and the way she was treated back then was different. Cameron just wants to get to know Avery and understand her, but he can't do it if he won't get answers from Avery herself. <br /><br />Avery knows she needs to stay away from Cameron, but she can't seem to mainly because of him. He keeps coming into her life without caring what she thinks because he simply wants to form a friendship with her. She can't seem to stay away from his sense of humor, from his thoughtful charm, and from the way he acts with her. Maybe being with Cameron is the best for them since he's able to be himself around her, able to bring the good side of him around her. He doesn't act the same around Avery than he does with others, but instead he acts like the caring and sweet loving guy he is. Trying to show his caring side to Avery, Cameron won't give up on getting the one chance he knows will change his life.<br /><br />What Cameron doesn't know about Avery is her past, and she doesn't want him to know. He suspects something, but he doesn't know. She's received texts and emails and calls that are threats and even though Cameron knows he shouldn't get involved, he tends to get involved <i>because he wants to help Avery and understand her.</i> Maybe allowing Cameron to help her would be for the best...<br /><br />I'd like to start this off with Cameron Hamilton. Cam, as he is called in this book, was probably the most swoon-worthy male lead I have ever read. There's reasons for that, and I'll get to that. Cameron is different than other NA male leads. He tends to take his time with Avery and not rush her into anything. He tends to care about her in any way possible because that's what he does, care about her. He tends to ask her permission to do something because he wants to make sure she's okay with it. And he tends to call her sweetheart instead of babe or baby and I found that utterly adorable.<br /><br />Cam has been added to many book boyfriends lists, and I don't blame those people. Of course, he's added to mine, along with so many others, but this one was a different kind of book boyfriend. It's the kind that I wish was real because of how charming and thoughtful he actually was with Avery. He showed his good side to her and when he was around her, he admitted things to her that she didn't think she would hear. Other than having beautiful and shimmering blue eyes, having the typical masculine body most NA males have including broad shoulders and a body that makes girls do things + broad shoulders and cheekbones, Cameron had a sweet, nice and soft spot with Avery that he didn't have with anyone else. He's got the perfect personality and sense of humour that any girl would want. What more would a girl ask for? When I said he asks Avery for her permission to make sure she's okay with what he's doing, I mean <i>he actually asks her if it's okay to take off her bra and to kiss her and to do things with her.</i> Ya know, those typical steamy and hot things. He was caring with her by making sure she was okay and taking care of her, worrying about her and making sure she was okay. He took his time with her, not rushing anything and not wanting her to rush anything because he wanted everything to be a way they both wanted it to be.<br /><br />The other thing about Cameron is that he was able to show his funny side to Avery. The way he would deliver his conversation with Avery was just so cute and it had me giggling so many times. He's hilarious! How could I not love the guy? Also, I mentioned he called her sweetheart since the beginning? I found that to be so cute as well. He called her Avery when it was serious, but the whole "sweetheart" thing was just so cute, I couldn't get over it. Cam was different than other guys because he actually asked Avery to go out on <i>a date</i> with him even though he knew he was in love with Avery already. I don't think insta love was involved, at least it didn't seem like it, but Cam did admit he was in love with her before he even knew it... Even with that being said, I loved how he kept asking her to go on a date with him and even when she said no over and over again, rejecting him again and again, he kept trying. He kept saying there was always tomorrow and that he can only hope, even when she said the answer was not going to change, I knew it was going to change. Obviously, the time where Avery would say yes to his question would come along sometimes, I was just waiting. He was so understandable and didn't care what her past was. I mean, of course, he showed his affectionate side and cared what happened, but he didn't love her any differently because of it. He loved her even more and was even more worried, but the way he was with her was just the best part of it. There wasn't one moment where Cam was mentioned or in that didn't have me giggling or squealing like a stupid little fangirl. <i>Well, that is what I am so it makes sense.</i><br /><br />Avery was different and an interesting character. I didn't see where she was coming from when the novel started, but I was able to understand her after. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I didn't think she was raped, but I knew something was wrong. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Although I didn't expect this, I knew there had to be something similar in a way. Avery's character was hard to get into at first. I didn't feel a connection with her throughout the whole book, but I was able to understand her. I did feel tears coming along because every time I read a book that has to do with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape or abuse, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I tend to get emotional. It just really bugs me how something horrific like that could happen especially to someone so young. No matter what the age is, it's something I hate reading about. It's just one of my biggest triggers even though I've read a couple of novels that involve either one of those or both. Avery's character was a little similar to those other characters in other books. She acted differently because of what happened and even if it was 5 years ago, there really isn't a way that person could forget about it. It's something that was, not haunting her, but something she couldn't forget. Her character made me sad sometimes, especially the way she acted with Cam at times when they were about to have sex or were making out. It was sad to hear her whole story but I'm glad she opened up to Cam and told her everything, expecting him to have a whole different reaction to the one he had. <br /><br />Her character changed throughout the book but what I loved about her was her sense of humor as well. She was able to bring Cam happiness and joy and laughter with her laughter and happiness. It was all just a bundle of happiness and joy. This wasn't a happy book, but most of it was. There were a lot of moments with Cam and Avery where they would have me laughing because of how cute they were and also because of how perfect they were together. They both understood each other so well and the way Cam came into Avery's life only to make it better was really all I needed to read about. Avery was able to change, for the better, and I was glad J. Lynn made her development better than what I expected. Although I hated her at times because <i>of how she acted with Cam,</i> I was able to understand why. The whole bracelet and wrist thing made me sad, but it was understandable. It brought her memories or it just made an effect on her, just like the time they were about to have a steamy moment but they both broke away from each other because Avery's mind went back to that cold night, only bringing back those awful memories she didn't want to think about. Avery went through a lot, I know that, and I although I don't know what it's like, I can see why she was how she was. It was hard for her to get a new start even with her 2 new friends and boyfriend. She was interesting, but she wasn't complex.<br /><br />I've said this many times, but I'm not the biggest fan of NA romance. I'm a bigger fan of reading how it's actually going to work out and reading about the dramatic drama. Of course, an NA novel needs to have 2 characters that both have something they are running away from or trying to change. If they didn't, there wouldn't be any drama behind it. J. Lynn created the perfect pair for this first novel, and I'm satisfied with it all. The romance was <b>steamy and hot</b> which is typical in NA novels, but this one was one of the only ones I was able to read without laughing because of how hilarious the scenes were described. Like I said, Cam asked Avery for her permission and that is part of the reason I <i>enjoyed</i> their "steamy moments." After knowing what happened to her, he asked her if it was okay to take her bra off, to kiss her in parts and to <i>touch her</i> which I found cute because he wanted to make sure she was okay. <br /><br />I <b>loved</b> how, like I said, Cam loved Avery even more after she told him the truth. It was just so wonderful to see someone love their love even more because of their past. I don't even know if that sounds right, but I'm just glad Cam was able to look at Avery the same no matter what happened in the past. I love how Jennifer created this male lead and let me just say, if the rest are like Cameron, I will definitely be swooning over the whole series and males and pairs and pretty much everything by Jennifer. I had doubts about Jennifer's writing before reading her Lux series, and boy I shouldn't have doubted her. <br /><br />The problem with this is that, like many other NA novels, <i>it felt like I have read this before.</i> <b>Different characters</b> told from <b>different perspectives</b>, but a lot of NA novels have to do with drama that has been told in other books but in different ways. I didn't really have expectations, not until I was beginning to suspect something was wrong with Avery, but I also didn't find it to be boring. Like I said, the book was actually pretty funny and fun to read thanks to Cam. Other than that, it was the typical NA novel. The reason I said it felt different is because of <b>the characters.</b> Luckily, JLA managed to created characters I didn't feel myself bored in and was able to like after understanding both.<br /><br />Jennifer has not become one of my favorites, but her writing is something I enjoy reading. It's something that can actually get me out of a reading slump because it's so easy to follow no matter what the book is about and where it's set. Her writing is the kind of writing I enjoy, easy to follow and enjoyable, and if it continues in the rest of the series, I'll definitely be considering her one of my favorite authors. I don't even know how she managed to do it but <b>she creates the perfect male leads.</b> I completely fell in love with Daemon in the Lux series, starting from Opal because I hated him in Obsidian and slightly disliked him in Onyx, but then I was like <i>BOY why can't you be real?</i> It's just the way she creates them, caring so passionately about their girlfriend or the girl they're in love with or whatever. <br /><br />Overall, the ending was also something I was satisfied with. There wasn't a cliffhanger, although there was a little snippet of Jase and Theresa (<i>mostly Jase thinking which gets me wondering why</i>). I'm excited to read the next book and finish the series, especially the next book which is about Theresa Hamilton and Jase Winstead, Cam's younger sister and best friend. Cam and Avery are a favorite couple of mine for sure and I know I will miss Cam's cute attitude with Avery, but I'm sure they will appear or pop up in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12664637255179581033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2952683200964046381">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>WARNING: I HAAAAAAAAAAAAATED THIS BOOK WITH A FIERY PASSION. </a><br/><br/>On motherf-ing page <b>THREE</b> we have our meet/cute where the girl literally runs into the boy and I discover this story will be one of my most hated of all tropes – a “superbadawful happened long long ago that new love interest will magically fix with all of hi</span>
  <span id="freeText2952683200964046381" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>WARNING: I HAAAAAAAAAAAAATED THIS BOOK WITH A FIERY PASSION. IF YOU LOVED IT, YOU PROBABLY WON’T LIKE THIS REVIEW. ALSO – THERE WILL BE SPOILERS.</b><br><br>Still here? Alrighty then . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447690937ra/17038250.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>On motherf-ing page <b>THREE</b> we have our meet/cute where the girl literally runs into the boy and I discover this story will be one of my most hated of all tropes – a “superbadawful happened long long ago that new love interest will magically fix with all of his wonderfulness as well as his magic penis.” <br><br>By page thirty girl and boy have discovered they have class together, have been paired up as partners in said class, realized they are also neighbors (how convenient), and that boy must be a werewolf because he’s always half naked . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447688999ra/17038059.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And while we don’t learn <i>exactly</i> what the superbadawful was, we do learn that the MC moved across the country in order to get away from the rumor mill in her hometown and that the alleged perpetrator’s name was <b>Blaine</b> . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447688999ra/17038060.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Exactly. <br><br>We then run through 11,842 pages of <b>NOTHING!</b> Well okay, not nothing. We have a female lead who obviously has some form of PTSD and <b>severe</b> trust issues, but who is always 100% willing to put herself in potentially unsafe situations by hanging out solo with the new neighbor. Uhhhhh, ever heard of Ted Bundy you dumb twat? Just ‘cause he’s good looking doesn’t mean he isn’t interested in murdering you while pretending you’re going to be working on Astronomy homework together. We also have a male MC who has a reputation for being a real panty dropper and proves he is such by calling our female lead “sweetheart” (vomit) constantly and by making her eggs on Sundays without even asking for a handjob first . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447688999ra/17038061.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But there’s still a <b>LOT</b> of nothing except pining away and what had to be a <b>horrific</b> case of blueballs which eventually culminates in the big moment when the dude finally got his payoff in the form of our leading lady’s V-Card. (Turns out only her butt virginity was taken from her by the perp, so score one for the new boy-next-door *eye roll*.) Which leads to the best moment of the entire book – UNPROTECTED FIRST TIME SEX. Oh, what a joy that was to read . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447688999ra/17038062.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book was a pile of shit. It not only wasted WAAAAAY too much of my precious reading time on a bunch of filler, but it was the <b>worst</b> example of what “romance” should be based on. Dear Authors, <b>STOP</b> romanticizing rape and making a big ol’ peen be the cure-all for these f*&amp;^ed up girls and their mental problems. As for this particular story????<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447689183ra/17038106.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The worst part is I really have no one to blame but myself since I totally had a “challenge accepted” moment and agreed to buddy read this turd. <div id="review_562713133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/562713133" />
    <a title="~ Becs ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2626261-becs"><img alt="~ Becs ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388693144p2/2626261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/562713133?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~ Becs ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~ Becs ~" href="/user/show/2626261-becs">~ Becs ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=abused-heroine">abused-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=tattooed-hero">tattooed-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=cover-lust-i-has-it">cover-lust-i-has-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=shy-heroine">shy-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562713133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4338652018844477366">I’m dusting off that seldom used fifth star for this one – it really is that good! I'm doing happy Jumping Jacks with glittery pom poms!!<br/><br/>I think it’s fair to say that my relationship with New Adult Romance has been rocky, at best. It promised me so much but, after a few casual and fun dates, I got burned by a bad book, totally betrayed by a hero that promised to be gorgeous, alpha and protective but ended up being a hero that I just wanted to throw rocks at and I retreated to lick my wounds so, </span>
  <span id="freeText4338652018844477366" style="display:none">I’m dusting off that seldom used fifth star for this one – it really is that good! I'm doing happy Jumping Jacks with glittery pom poms!!<br /><br />I think it’s fair to say that my relationship with New Adult Romance has been rocky, at best. It promised me so much but, after a few casual and fun dates, I got burned by a bad book, totally betrayed by a hero that promised to be gorgeous, alpha and protective but ended up being a hero that I just wanted to throw rocks at and I retreated to lick my wounds so, yeah, me and New Adult – we’ve been on a break, a trial separation as it were.<br /><br />It hasn’t been easy – temptation is everywhere and then, there was Wait For You making eyes at me with it’s Adam Levine lookalike cover model, flashing its five star reviews at me and generally saying ‘Come on baby, you know you want to’. I’m a cautious soul, I tried to look the other way but another blogger whose judgement I trust, (Nat, that’s you flower) dropped it into a book conversation we were having and I found my resistance crumbling and I slowly, tentatively reached out and Wait For You grabbed me by the hand and ran ahead with me stumbling along in its wake, slightly dazed.<br /><br />And dazed is the right word because Wait For You is just all kinds of awesome – full of goofy grin loveliness, I read this with a big cheesy smile on my face. It had a kind of magnetic hold on me – every time I tried to put it down I was sucked straight back in. Just. Could. Not. Put. It. Down!<br /><br />So we’re right back on college campus, hotbed of new adult romances, with Avery and Cam, who could most definitely relight my fire, slowly getting to know one another. Avery has travelled right across the country to go to college but more importantly to get away from her past and her family. She has a secret which has far reaching consequences over her decision making and the way she lives her life today and this secret is only slowly revealed throughout the novel – it’s drip fed to us gradually. Yes, you can guess but not the specifics and it held my curiosity all through the story.<br /><br /><br />Avery kind of broke my heart at the beginning - she just seemed so very alone. She had plenty of coping mechanisms to get her through the day but she’s not really living, just moving on from one day to the next. I felt so sorry for her – the people that should have been there to cherish her and care for her had really let her down when she needed them most and she’s reached the point where she trusts no one and cannot comprehend why people are now being nice to her.<br /><br />She literally crashes into Cam on her way to her very first class and it soon transpires that they are neighbours and they get to know each other slowly. Cam – le sigh!! Cam is just wonderful. Every girl needs a Cam. He’s funny, charming, endearingly over-confident, thoughtful, attentive, caring and HOT – I could continue to rain down superlatives but I think you get the gist, right? I pretty much adored him right from the get go. I loved the way he asked Avery to go out with him on an almost daily basis – he never gave up and just waited for her to slowly come around even though she took hard to get to a whole new level.<br /><br />This is very much a character driven novel, there’s really no pulsating action plot. The two main characters take things very slowly, plenty of time is given to building their characters and their relationships and I really felt like I’d got to know them very well and it felt completely believable. Never once did my attention waver: I was thoroughly engrossed from beginning to end and I completely lost a whole day in this novel and I really can’t think of a better way to have spent it!<br /><br /><br />Trust is the central theme here – Avery will need to learn to trust Cam and her reticence will threaten to destroy their fledgling relationship.Trust has not and will not come easily to Avery and it’s going to be a rocky journey for her – she knows that to move forward she will have to learn to trust Cam with her secrets but will she be able to? Will she allow the love that is growing between Cam and herself heal the wounds left by the demons of her past or will she let her old fears shadow the warmth she shares with him?<br /><br />So, this is a beautiful new adult romance - it’s captivating, engaging and very romantic. I adored both Cam and Avery as well as Avery’s new friends Brittany and Jacob, Cam’s friend Ollie plus the long-suffering turtle/tortoise (not sure what it was) Raphael. There’s a whole gang of characters to laugh with, cry with and just fall in love with. I have to thank J Lynn (who is actually Jennifer L Armentrout) as she has pretty much restored my faith in the new adult genre and we’re dating again now. I feel more hopeful again. It’s a beautiful thing!<br /><br />I will share this with you. It really has nothing to do with the story, more my own experience in reading it. in particular the following sentence.<br /><br /><b>After showering, I piddled around the apartment and debated texting Jacob or Brittany to see what they were up to.</b><br /><br />This is one of the pitfalls of being a British reviewer reading mostly American books. In that sentence, we would probably say I pottered around the apartment because to piddle over here means to pee and I had this bizarre mental image of Avery peeing in all four corners of her apartment, fastidiously marking her territory!! I laughed like a drain (British expression!!) and actually scared my cat off my lap!!<br /><br />Anyway I digress, this is a very special new adult romance and I’m going to highly recommend it to all of our followers. It’s endearing and quite simply unputdownable. Is that a word? Well, it is now!<br /><br /><br />5 big shiny stars<br /><br /><i>For more reviews, please visit <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Reviews</a> or visit us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4338652018844477366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_566062566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566062566" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/566062566?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=e-version">e-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=wring-her-neck">wring-her-neck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=self-published">self-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=i-cannot-tell-you-my-secret">i-cannot-tell-you-my-secret</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=sex-and-glamour">sex-and-glamour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=caries-promotingly-sweet">caries-promotingly-sweet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=new-adult-fiction">new-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer566062566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer827370548347952595"><i>**** If it is possible to spoil a story that has practically no mentionable plot and no mystery, but makes do with a certain set of formulaic elements (see farther below), spinning them in circles to make the experience last longer, then be warned: Spoilers line the rocky road ****</i><br/><br/>I am seldom that outspoken, but in this case I just have to say it aloud - probably all the 'fucks' and 'shits' the characters flung about celebrating their verbal New Adult freedom rubbed off on me: In my opinion "Wai</span>
  <span id="freeText827370548347952595" style="display:none"><i>**** If it is possible to spoil a story that has practically no mentionable plot and no mystery, but makes do with a certain set of formulaic elements (see farther below), spinning them in circles to make the experience last longer, then be warned: Spoilers line the rocky road ****</i><br /><br />I am seldom that outspoken, but in this case I just have to say it aloud - probably all the 'fucks' and 'shits' the characters flung about celebrating their verbal New Adult freedom rubbed off on me: In my opinion "Wait for You" is <i>utter shit</i> and I don't understand in the least why people enjoy spending time on it. My expectations had been rather low after reading "Obsidian", but probably they were not low enough.<br /><br />So, let's see: Former, rich, unkissed social pariah Avery enrolls in a small no-name college to start a new, normal life far from home and literally bumps into Cameron-I-Had-Them-All-And-They-Liked-It, but because of her past and her personality it takes him a few months to tease a date out of the one girl who resists and her four months of heavy-duty petting <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He never even asks why. Maybe he thinks it's "the traditional virgin way"? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and a few mental break-downs to admit she has a problem - a problem of unbelievable proportions, which the reader has pretty much puzzled together since chapter 1 or 2 or 3. That's it! Have a go at guessing! You cannot fail. The quotes are all to be found in the first 11% of the book, most of them on the very first pages:<br /><br /><b>Reaching down, I checked the wide, silver bracelet on my wrist, making sure it was in place.</b><br /><br /><b>A guy had never held me. I didn't count that one time, because that time didn't count for shit.</b><br /><br /><b>Parties didn't end well for me. </b><br /><br /><b>I hadn't been able to see a possible after when the entire school got behind Blaine.</b><br /><br /><b>Nothing could have been worse than what had happened to me, what my parents agreed to.</b><br /><br /><b>Apparently my parents were okay with having a daughter labeled a lying whore.</b><br /><br />The paragraphs that are <i>not</i> dripping with hints to her - or his - tragic past or with sexual activity consist of artificial, middle-school-level-immature conversations the heroine has with her new cardboard friends - i.e.: <br /><br /><b><i>'Cam?'</i> Brittany blinked. 'Yeah?' [...] Brittany's brows knitted. 'People who he doesn't know call him Cameron. Only his friends call him Cam.' 'Oh.' I frowned. 'He told me people call him Cam, so I assumed that's what people called him.'</b> <br /><br />and oily, self-gratifying banter orchestraed by Mr. Let-Me-Bake-For-You-Sweetheart out to seduce an iron virgin:<br /><br /><b>'So unless you were raised in a convent, I imagined you've been in a lap a time or two, right?'</b><br /><br /><b>'I'm a lot to handle, but I can assure you, you'll have fun handling me.'</b><br /><br />To be frank, after schlepping myself through this highly praised, much-squealed-about example that has even been practically fought over by international licence buyers, I do not have much hope left for the genre and its ability to bring forth something I can enjoy and I don’t really believe anymore that <br /><br />- there is a New Adult novel without <u>a heroine who suffered some kind of abuse</u> before meeting creation's finest in form of the hero. I cannot believe how rape or almost-rape or abusive parental behavior has been quickly established as one of the truly unavoidable requirements for a successfully hot tear-jerker romance.<br />- there is a New Adult novel without <u>a heroine who is sexually inexperienced</u> or unable to let go sexually <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In "Wait for You" the author has combined the rape <i>and</i> the virgin factor by a desperate coup de force that is so ridiculous you cannot help but applaud in awe: Avery’s abuser had raped her by going the anal route. And than means hymen-wise our heroine is still pure and extra-virgin despite her defining earlier experience  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but is oh so attractive to the hero and secretly special and siren-like seductive under the layers of her tragic past.<br />- there is a New Adult novel without <u>a hero who is prone to violent outbursts</u> directed towards people who deserve it, but tender and protective as far as the fragile heroine is concerned.<br />- there is a New Adult novel without <u>a hero who had been consuming girls like breakfast</u> - and is universally admired for that because his sex skills are too advanced to be wasted on one woman only - but who changes his habit from 100 to zero, because wanting the heroine so bad made him lose his appetite for even the most appealing piece of ass on legs.<br />- there is a New Adult hero who is not filthily rich or at least <u>in possession of a convenient amount of money </u>in form of a trust fund, royalties, or a well-paying business he started at an astonishing young age.<br />- there is a New Adult novel in which the characters are really on their way to become thinking, independent grown-ups instead of being <u>closet High Schoolers playing College </u>with a drawer full of condoms and a key to their own apartment or trailer.<br /><br />In the light of "Wait for You" and its equally awful chronies I think have to be fair and eventually take all the titles I enthusiastically added to my New Adult shelf last year (i.e. "Holier than Thou", "The Piper's Son", „Where She Went“, "Raw Blue", "Come and See Me" ...), when the genre began to coin itself, off again. For in my opinion it counts as an affront to those titles to be grouped together with books that fulfill the above mentioned basic prerequisites - which really I cannot stand to come across anymore. <br /><br />Recently I accidentally noticed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Let me assure you: I did not actively seek it out <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> the description for Armentrout’s upcoming novel "Frigid": <b>
  <i>"... Kyler puts the 'man' in man-whore ... has always put Syd on a pedestal that was too high for him to reach ... there's nothing stopping their red-hot feelings for each other ..."<i></i></i>
</b> and I thought: Shove it back into the eighteenth century, squeeze her into a tight, but demure corset, hand him an inheritance and a full stamp card of a small-town discount bordello and you've got a regular bodice ripper (I know: There is nothing wrong with those. But everybody knows at least what to expect from historical romance). What is "new"(=different) in New Adult fiction is only the contemporary setting and that strange fixation on sexual abuse.<br /><br />I am astonished by my own thoughts, but I guess I would rather stick to good old British ChickLit when searching for a realistic story about a young woman finding her place in life and a guy to suck up to than to suffer more of this vile, repetitive and uneventful stuff. Unfortunately I have already "Slammed" and "Easy" on my Kindle and thus I believe I will venture into the jungle of damaged girls and hot, temperamental boy-men at least twice again <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At the moment I cannot imagine making it through to the end, though. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Sad, sad business, I know. So don't kill me for my opinion. I suffered enough reading the book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="827370548347952595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1940999982" />
    <a title="KAS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20691061-kas"><img alt="KAS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472348331p2/20691061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1940999982?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KAS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KAS" href="/user/show/20691061-kas">KAS</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1940999982" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14409466369950985575">4.25 Stars<br/><br/><b>A SLOW BURN TO THE NTH DEGREE</b> <br/><br/>I love the NA genre and have been wanting to read something by this author. As soon as I started the first chapter, I knew I was in for a treat.<br/><br/>The MC's, Avery and Cam, were exactly what I hoped for. Avery is sassy, determined and says whatever she feels like, but is emotionally flawed. Cam is adorably full of himself, fun to be around, and oh so confident and sinfully gorgeous. <br/><br/>Girls clamor to be with Cam, but he sets his sights on the red-headed beauty, </span>
  <span id="freeText14409466369950985575" style="display:none">4.25 Stars<br /><br /><b>A SLOW BURN TO THE NTH DEGREE</b> <br /><br />I love the NA genre and have been wanting to read something by this author. As soon as I started the first chapter, I knew I was in for a treat.<br /><br />The MC's, Avery and Cam, were exactly what I hoped for. Avery is sassy, determined and says whatever she feels like, but is emotionally flawed. Cam is adorably full of himself, fun to be around, and oh so confident and sinfully gorgeous. <br /><br />Girls clamor to be with Cam, but he sets his sights on the red-headed beauty, named Avery, and makes a constant pest out of himself until she agrees to go on a date with him. Stubborn to a fault, Avery soon learns the hard way, she can't live without him.<br /><br /> <i>"Don't you have anyone else to bother?"</i><br /><br /> <i>"There are a shit ton of people that I could reward with my presence, but I chose you."</i><br /><br />I could not get enough of these two, and their lively, bantering conversations. Their chemistry is undeniably sizzling and their relationship is quite angsty. I love a slow burn romance, and this one had it in spades.<br /><br />A snippet of the storyline ......<br /><br />Avery Morgansten selects a college nearly across the country to get away from her parents and her hometown. She needed to go to a place where she knew no one and no one knew her. A place totally different from her high school days where everyone hated her. A place where she wasn't called a 'whore' and 'liar.' A place where she could start over and let go of the past, unfortunately the past doesn't want to let go of her.<br /><br />Running late to her very first college class, she literally collides into 'the' Cameron Hamilton. Later that evening, she discovers she moved into the same apartment complex he lives in and is just across the hall. He is overly flirty and extremely easy on the eyes. Speaking of eyes, his are the deepest blue she has ever seen. <br /><br /> <i>"He was gorgeous in all the ways that made girls do stupid things."</i><br /><br />Although Avery is nineteen and a freshman in college, she doesn't do stupid things with guys. She has never been in a relationship before, never dated, never had her first real kiss. Cam makes it completely obvious he hopes to change all that, but Avery knows he would be way too much for her to handle. She hopes someday she can start dating and lead a normal life, because 'normal' was taken away from her on Halloween night five years ago by an older boy named Blaine.<br /><br />Cam, who doesn't have a shy bone in his body, is totally intrigued by Avery. She is extremely pretty, but doesn't flaunt it. She is smart and witty, but refuses to go out with him, which makes him all the more determined. He is also at a loss for why she keeps turning him down, because girls don't turn him down. She was proving to be quite the challenge, and he was intrigued enough to play the game. He also knows she is holding her past close to the vest, but understands all too well, as he has his own secrets he would rather not discuss.<br /><br />Unfortunately, relationships don't last when secrets are kept.<br /><br />If you enjoy a slow burn romance, and believe you me, this was s.l.o.w. b.u.r.n., I think you will like this one.<br /><br />This story was written in Avery's POV. I am anxious to read Cam's POV in "Trust In Me" next. Knowing Cam, it is going to be quite interesting and fun!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14409466369950985575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12372238702255119453"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380407931i/797373.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4.5 swoonworthy stars! New-Adult romance at its best!</b><br/>My Cameron and Avery:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380407931i/797374.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Avery</b> is starting college, far away from her home, ever critical parents and her past. She wants just one single thing - to start over and have a normal life with noone knowing what had happened to her five years ago when she was only fourteen and what made her closed and uncomfortable around others. But what she is not expecting is Cameron - popular, extremely good looking and real charmer who is determined to get to know</span>
  <span id="freeText12372238702255119453" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380407931i/797373.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4.5 swoonworthy stars! New-Adult romance at its best!</b><br>My Cameron and Avery:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380407931i/797374.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Avery</b> is starting college, far away from her home, ever critical parents and her past. She wants just one single thing - to start over and have a normal life with noone knowing what had happened to her five years ago when she was only fourteen and what made her closed and uncomfortable around others. But what she is not expecting is Cameron - popular, extremely good looking and real charmer who is determined to get to know her better. But will Avery be able to run away from her past forever?<br><br>I just love books in which I can gradually reveal what had happened to characters and shaped them the way they are now. Wait For You maybe isn't the most unique story ever written but I enjoyed every single word of it. I had a huge smile on my face most of the time and I was <b>completely smitten by hero - Cam</b>. <br><br>Oh, Cam... he was smart, funny and sexy. A very dangerous combination! I fell for him in a matter of couple chapters. He was confident, determined, sometimes cocky but never a jerk. On contrary, he was really nice and caring person. Perfection, right? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> just knows the best how to write truly swoonworthy heroes. Moreover, Avery was sweet, smart and adorably akward. Yeah, she was a coward, ignoring her problems most of the time but otherwise a very lovable heroine. Together, Cam and Avery created another fictional couple I grew to love and felt strongly compassionate about.<br><br>Wait For You is about finding something in your life which is wort of facing your problems instead of running away from them. Wait For You is about coming to terms with decisions and concequences you are not proud about and finally being able to move on. <b>Wait For You is beautiful and emotional page-turner in which Jennifer L. Armentrout proved what a perfect writer she is. I LOVED IT IMMENSELY!</b><br><br><a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1216803265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216803265" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1216803265?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062294777" href="/book/show/17754041-wait-for-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=smutty">smutty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216803265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3139926970680690718">2.5 stars<br/><br/>Trigger Warning: Rape<br/><br/>Aight.... So I'm in the middle of literally like 6 books and last night i was like U KNOW WHAT I JUST NEED SOMETHING EASY AND LIGHT AND FUN AND SMUTTY SO HECK IT I'M GONNA READ THIS and i promptly read it in 2 sittings before i went to bed and right when i woke up. <br/><br/>A history of my and JLA's relationship: I was obsessed with the Luxe series when I was like 15 but stopped liking them after book 3 when it got too smutty and weird. I've read a few of her more recent nov</span>
  <span id="freeText3139926970680690718" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />Trigger Warning: Rape<br /><br />Aight.... So I'm in the middle of literally like 6 books and last night i was like U KNOW WHAT I JUST NEED SOMETHING EASY AND LIGHT AND FUN AND SMUTTY SO HECK IT I'M GONNA READ THIS and i promptly read it in 2 sittings before i went to bed and right when i woke up. <br /><br />A history of my and JLA's relationship: I was obsessed with the Luxe series when I was like 15 but stopped liking them after book 3 when it got too smutty and weird. I've read a few of her more recent novels, but I just think her writing style is corny and her dialogue and characters are unrealistic, so I knew going into this that I wasn't going to like it, but it would still be fast and addicting.<br /><br />I was right. <br />I did an instagram livestream while I read ~30 pages of this book and I was just making fun of it out loud because for the first half of this book, there were literally several things PER PAGE that made me go UGGHGGHGHHGHGHGHHHH<br /><br />Here's a list of those things, as well as some other problematic content I noticed:<br />-the only gay character in the book is constantly sexualizing other men and saying "girl" and "honey" at the beginning of every sentence. Sometimes stereotypes are true, but it was just really uncomfortable for JLA to establish that one of her characters is gay by making him BLATANTLY. GAY.<br />-woop, there it is. only took 60 pages for male character to say "you're not like most girls." Later on in the text, he tells her that she's "Different in a good kind of way." yikes.<br />-the amount of times that Cam has to catch her or pick up things for her or buckle her goddamn seatbelt for her is so annoying. let the girl live. at one point he buttoned her coat for her when she was perfectly capable of doing it and it was just so infantilizing. women can do shit by themselves leave us the fuck alone<br />-so much problematic..<br /> -JLA commonly referred to certain characters as "fucktard." it was meant as a joke, but the variation on the word "retard" could be considered offensive.<br /> -At one point a couple of the characters juggled around the phrase, "I'd go gay for you," implying that being gay is a choice, not something you're born with.<br /> -The main character refers to someone as "spaz," and I know some people with disabilities are uncomfortable with that word being used as a slur.<br /><br />One of my main issues in this is that Cam (love interest dude) asked her out. every day. for two months. that's uncomfortable, and that's harassment. jla posing it as a "joke" in this books just normalizes that girls should let themselves be treated like this and consider it a joke. furthermore, her friends bully and peer pressure her into going out with him. any time he would be like, "hey, come with me to this thing," her friends would LITERALLY say stuff like "i'll punch you in the face if you don't go." Again, posing it as a joke just makes it even more disturbing. <br /><br />Additionally, I just really didn't like JLA's message about rape and rapists. A lot of this book focused on Avery overcoming her trauma of being raped, but in the end, nothing happened to the rapist? She dropped the charges, never thought about testifying, and no one in this book encouraged her to tell the truth or go to the police. I just thought this aspect of the book was done really frustratingly and unrealistically, and I was disappointed to see that the way she "moved on" from it all wasn't to contact the police and get justice, but just to be like "from now on, **I** control my life, and no one will tell me otherwise!!" and I just don't think that's a realistic portrayal of how women overcome trauma, especially if their rapist is still on the loose.<br /><br />The reason this didn't get one or two stars, however, is because I gotta give it to JLA. Although this book was so corny it had my eyes rolling for 90% of it, I gotta admit that she knows how to write slow-burning love scenes. I think there's a really, really great basis for a heartfelt story here, but if I was her editor, I would have her fix a lot of the annoying and problematic dialogue and inner monologue, then it would be so much better. But needless to say, I couldn't put this book down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3139926970680690718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8664516751757094505"> <b>+5 COOKIES STARS <3<br/><br/><br/>""Are you sure?" "I have cookies."<br/>"Cookies?"<br/>"Yeah, and I made them.I'm quite the baker."</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404088282ra/10189716.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Amazing!!!I loved it so much!It was beautiful, emotional and at many parts hilarious!!I didn't want to finished reading it, the story was so addictive!And the part about the cookies...omg :)) It was hilarious!!!I will definately eat Cam's cookies!!!<br/><br/>The book starts with Avery who was seeking a new life and she goes from Texas in a college to West Virginia.Something bother her from her past.</span>
  <span id="freeText8664516751757094505" style="display:none"> <b>+5 COOKIES STARS &lt;3<br><br><br>""Are you sure?" "I have cookies."<br>"Cookies?"<br>"Yeah, and I made them.I'm quite the baker."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404088282ra/10189716.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Amazing!!!I loved it so much!It was beautiful, emotional and at many parts hilarious!!I didn't want to finished reading it, the story was so addictive!And the part about the cookies...omg :)) It was hilarious!!!I will definately eat Cam's cookies!!!<br><br>The book starts with Avery who was seeking a new life and she goes from Texas in a college to West Virginia.Something bother her from her past..so she she's introvert.But things will change when literally crashed in a handsome boy in the first day to school...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403459288i/10095883._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cam is opposite of Avery!He is very communicative and everybody knows him..when he meets Avery he wants to date her...<br><br> <b>“You want to say yes, but you’re just not ready.”<br>My jaw dropped.<br>“It’s okay.” His grin turned cocky. “I’m a lot to handle, but I can assure you, you’ll have fun handling me.”</b><br><br>He has to wate a lot until she finally accepts his offer :) The chemistry between them was so sweet and hilarious!I absolutely loved them together!!Cam is exactly what Avery needs!What I loved more about their relationship was that first they start as friends and then they fell in love and it was so real!! *sigh* Cam showed all his emotions,something that we don't see often in male characters!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403459288ra/10095884.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The story wasn't something that I haven't read before,however Jennifer's writing was amazing that made it unique!<br><br>Avery was sweet,funny,charming and smart!There were moments that she irritated me but in general I liked her!Cam,Cam,Cam....omg I loved him!!!He was amazing!He is definately one of my top book boyfriends!He was so adorable,hot,sweet,funny and so patient with Avery!I think he is exactly what a girl needs!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404201036i/10206999._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> If you are a fan of Jennifer and you like slow building friendships that blossoms in a relationships then this is exactly what you need!!I'm looking forward to read the second book!!<br> <b>As for Cam's book,I'm not sure yet if I will read it because I had said that I will not read again this type of books with the different POV but honestly I can't resist another book with Cam &lt;333 :)))<br><br>Please give me more Cam *sigh* :)))</b> <br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_986724495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/986724495" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406624675p2/31339793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/986724495?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jasmine by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=smartass-witty-banters">smartass-witty-banters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=swoon-worthy-guys">swoon-worthy-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=buddy-recs">buddy-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=i-love-me-some-angst-drama">i-love-me-some-angst-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=killing-me-with-sexual-tension">killing-me-with-sexual-tension</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=imma-hit-that-bitch">imma-hit-that-bitch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=fluffy-fluffer">fluffy-fluffer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=in-rachel-i-trust">in-rachel-i-trust</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer986724495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17626361278828136131"><b>3 - 3.5 COOKIE STARS! ★★★☆</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“I'm beginning to think cookies is a code word for something else."</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419948418ra/13149808.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yup. Don't think I'll ever see a cookie in the same way again ;D<br/><br/>Anywho. GAH I couldn't really settle with a rating for this one because the first half of the book felt like a solid 4, but the second half starting getting on my nerves with Avery. And there's Cam and his pet tortoise Raphael who I would give 5 stars to. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419949257ra/13149856.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The thing with NA reads is that it's very hard to please with all the recycled plot</span>
  <span id="freeText17626361278828136131" style="display:none"><b>3 - 3.5 COOKIE STARS! ★★★☆</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“I'm beginning to think cookies is a code word for something else."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419948418ra/13149808.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yup. Don't think I'll ever see a cookie in the same way again ;D<br><br>Anywho. GAH I couldn't really settle with a rating for this one because the first half of the book felt like a solid 4, but the second half starting getting on my nerves with Avery. And there's Cam and his pet tortoise Raphael who I would give 5 stars to. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419949257ra/13149856.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The thing with NA reads is that it's very hard to please with all the recycled plots and with this one, it's really no exception. This is a typical college romance where reformed hot player meets new girl in town running from a terrible past. They bumped into each other, guy tries to woo her and all that shenanigans that makes the recipe of a NA read. <br><br>I really enjoyed the first half of the book, the dialogues were highly entertaining and there's Cam with his cookies. Cam alone would have warrant 5 stars from me; he was just super sweet, caring, understanding that he is <i>literally</i> too perfect to be real. And ladies, HE BAKES! And he would cook eggs every Sunday morning for you! <br><br>But seriously tho, <b>HE BAKES COOKIES.</b> Chocolate and walnut cookies. <b>COOKIES EVERYWHERE.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411537ra/808566.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But then Avery, ah geez *facepalm* Usually I'm very tolerant and understanding of damaged heroines, but I got superbly ticked off with Avery when she constantly kept pushing away Cam. Who the f*ck says NO to a guy like Cam?! GAHH! <br><br>Also, it really doesn't help that the secret reveal of her past was dragged on forever till the end and frankly, that made it super difficult for me to be sympathetic for her throughout. She ended up coming off annoying for me after a good while because I wanted her actions to be damn well justified for acting that way. But nope, she just kept living in her little bubble. <br><br>I'm not even gonna lie but Avery really doesn't deserve him. Where is the justice in this world right now?! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419948040ra/13149756.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall it was still a nice sweet read but nothing phenomenal when it comes to the plot. It does have its emotional moments and a great addition of side characters. Cam definitely is the highlight of this book but a tiny part of me is mad that he could be so fixated on a girl like Avery. If it wasn't for Cam, I may have totally ditched this book. *sighs*<br><br><i>PS: Thanks Rachel for introducing Cam to me and ruining all men on the planet for me right now! ♥♥</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17626361278828136131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/549277615?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Michele" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Michele" href="/user/show/16809610-beth-michele">Beth Michele</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16809610-beth-michele?shelf=my-favs">my-favs</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer549277615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11126830748140518373">(Tapping my finger against the side of my head) Where to begin.<br/><br/>First off, I will never look at cookies and eggs the same way again. I love cookies, and if that's a code word for something else, then I'll take that too. Nor will I be able to eat them without thinking about CAM. Sigh. He was incredibly hot, right down to that sun tattoo, absolutely, but it was something more. It was his sense of humor (love that), his playfulness, his thoughtfulness. Loved during their intimate moments how he woul</span>
  <span id="freeText11126830748140518373" style="display:none">(Tapping my finger against the side of my head) Where to begin.<br /><br />First off, I will never look at cookies and eggs the same way again. I love cookies, and if that's a code word for something else, then I'll take that too. Nor will I be able to eat them without thinking about CAM. Sigh. He was incredibly hot, right down to that sun tattoo, absolutely, but it was something more. It was his sense of humor (love that), his playfulness, his thoughtfulness. Loved during their intimate moments how he would always ask "May I?" So incredibly sweet. Plus, I could totally picture him saying "Hell to the mother fucking no," and that is totally HOT! (knees scraping the floor, palms up, eyes wide)…..More please.<br /><br />LOVED all the playful banter. I’m a huge fan of it. There’s something about it. Perhaps it’s the way my whole face smiles while I’m reading it, or the way my mind wanders to the possibilities of the words and where they will take the characters, and me along with them. It’s flirty, it’s sexy, it’s...well, enough said.<br /><br />I was a bit angry at Avery for not opening up sooner and trusting Cam. Come on, the guy laid his heart out, among other things. She needed to do the same. However, the fact that everything wrapped up nicely in the end, and I got my happily ever after....made it all worthwhile.<br /><br />Now I'm off to have a cookie! :)<br /><br />ADDENDUM: Cam going commando...HOLY SH***!!!!!!<br /><br /> <br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=definitely-not-young-adult">definitely-not-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192343941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3350730093007790072"><br/>As my first ever JLA read, I have no idea as to what to expect. But simply basing it on friends’ reviews, I know for a fact that JLA is one of our elite kick-ass writers. This book made me see why. She is naturally endowed with great writing skills, so that although this entire story is quite a bit familiar (as it reminds me so much of a mix across Hopeless by Colleen Hoover, Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson and the Lovely Vicious series by Sara Wolf- all of which are great books, BTW), she still </span>
  <span id="freeText3350730093007790072" style="display:none"><br />As my first ever JLA read, I have no idea as to what to expect. But simply basing it on friends’ reviews, I know for a fact that JLA is one of our elite kick-ass writers. This book made me see why. She is naturally endowed with great writing skills, so that although this entire story is quite a bit familiar (as it reminds me so much of a mix across Hopeless by Colleen Hoover, Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson and the Lovely Vicious series by Sara Wolf- all of which are great books, BTW), she still managed to make it such an exciting read that it took me only a day to finish it. Her use of hilarious analogies and metaphors gets me all the time. The only thing that bothered me just a little is the abundant use of the f-word, like REALLY abundant ^^<br /><br />But though admittedly the entire story did not knock me off my feet, the characters (Cam most especially) thankfully did. He is simply perfection, totally a sweetheart! Just read the book and you’ll agree. Here’s a preview…<br /><br /><i> <b> “I’m serious about you, Avery. If you want me for real, you have me.” </b></i>  <br /><br />Avery is likable enough, although at one point I almost got tired of her for being too strained over her past. Good thing she’s surrounded by wonderful friends like Jacob (who’s kept me entertained) and Brit who is a darling and of course, Cam. Avery is sooooo lucky to have him. <br /><br /><i>
  <b> “I loved his belief in me. It was beautiful.” </b>
</i> <br /><br />I would have loved to have seen more than just a glimpse of her dancing though. I wish the author put more details about that .</span>
  <a data-text-id="3350730093007790072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
